## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of a non-linear harmonic oscillator. The equation of motion typically expresses acceleration as a sum of a restoring force (function of position x), a damping force (function of velocity v), and possibly an external driving force (function of time t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force (Hooke's law): dv_dt = c0 * x
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3
- Duffing with linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * x
- Rayleigh oscillator (cubic damping): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * x
- Quadratic fluid damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v)
- Pendulum equation: dv_dt = c0 * sin(x)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(x) + c1 * v
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t)
- Quintic stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5
- Nonlinear damping with displacement coupling: dv_dt = c0 * v * (1 - c1 * x**2) + c2 * x
- Coulomb (dry) friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sign(v) (sign(v) = v / Abs(v))
- Combined linear and cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3
- Forcing with cosine: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd monomials in position (x, x**3, x**5) indicate symmetric restoring forces with nonlinear stiffness (hardening/softening spring).
- Linear term in velocity (c * v) corresponds to classical viscous damping (energy dissipation).
- Quadratic velocity term v * Abs(v) models fluid drag damping at high Reynolds numbers (direction‑preserving dissipation).
- Self‑excitation term of the form v * (1 - c * x**2) is characteristic of Van der Pol‑type limit‑cycle oscillators.
- Sinusoidal time‑dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) represents external periodic forcing.
- Sign of velocity c * sign(v) represents dry Coulomb friction (constant force opposing motion).
- Coupling term x**2 * v signifies displacement‑dependent nonlinear damping (e.g., parametric excitation or amplitude‑dependent dissipation).
- Sine of displacement sin(x) appears in pendulum‑like oscillators, providing a periodic restoring force that reduces to ~x for small angles.
- Rayleigh‑type damping term v**3 describes a symmetric nonlinear damping that strongly penalizes large velocities.
- Asymmetric potential wells (e.g., quadratic stiffness term x**2) introduce a bias and break the odd symmetry of the restoring force.
